href="#cite_note-28June2017PR-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Activity</th><td class="infobox-data">Aerobatic displays<br />Static displays</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Organized by</th><td class="infobox-data">SIAE (<a href="/wiki/GIFAS" title="GIFAS">GIFAS</a>)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Website</th><td class="infobox-data"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.paris-air-show.com/">paris-air-show.com</a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>Paris Air Show</b> (<a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr"><b>Salon international de l\'a\xc3\xa9ronautique et de l\'espace de Paris-Le Bourget</b>, <b>Salon du Bourget</b></i>) is a <a href="/wiki/Trade_fair" title="Trade fair">trade fair</a> and air show held in odd years at <a href="/wiki/Paris%E2%80%93Le_Bourget_Airport" title="Paris\xe2\x80\x93Le Bourget Airport">Paris\xe2\x80\x93Le Bourget Airport</a> in north Paris, France. Organized by the French aerospace industry\'s primary representative body, the <i>Groupement des industries fran\xc3\xa7aises a\xc3\xa9ronautiques et spatiales</i> (<a href="/wiki/GIFAS" title="GIFAS">GIFAS</a>), it is the largest <a href="/wiki/Air_show" title="Air show">air show</a> and aerospace-industry exhibition event in the world, measured by number of exhibitors and size of exhibit space, followed by UK\'s <a href="/wiki/Farnborough_Air_Show" class="mw-redirect" title="Farnborough Air Show">Farnborough Air Show</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dubai_Air_Show" class="mw-redirect" title="Dubai Air Show">Dubai Air Show</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Airshow" title="Singapore Airshow">Singapore Airshow</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>First held in 1909,<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> the Paris Air Show was held every odd year from 1949 to 2019, when the 53rd Air Show attracted 2,453 exhibitors from 49 countries and occupied more than 125,000 square meters. Organizers canceled the 2021 show due to the COVID pandemic and said it would resume in 2023.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>It is a large <a href="/wiki/Trade_fair" title="Trade fair">trade fair</a>, demonstrating military and civilian aircraft, and is attended by many <a href="/wiki/Military_force" class="mw-redirect" title="Military force">military forces</a> and the major <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_manufacturer" class="mw-redirect" title="Aircraft manufacturer">aircraft manufacturers</a>, often announcing major aircraft sales.\nIt starts with four professional days and is then opened to the general public followed from Friday to Sunday.\nThe format is similar to Farnborough and the <a href="/wiki/ILA_Berlin_Air_Show" title="ILA Berlin Air Show">ILA Berlin Air Show</a>, both staged in even years.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paris_Air_Show&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Salon_de_locomotion_aerienne_1909_Grand_Palais_Paris.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f9/Salon_de_locomotion_aerienne_1909_Grand_Palais_Paris.jpg/220px-Salon_de_locomotion_aerienne_1909_Grand_Palais_Paris.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="171" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f9/Salon_de_locomotion_aerienne_1909_Grand_Palais_Paris.jpg/330px-Salon_de_locomotion_aerienne_1909_Grand_Palais_Paris.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f9/Salon_de_locomotion_aerienne_1909_Grand_Palais_Paris.jpg/440px-Salon_de_locomotion_aerienne_1909_Grand_Palais_Paris.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2808" data-file-height="2179" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Salon_de_locomotion_aerienne_1909_Grand_Palais_Paris.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The first <i>Salon de la locomotion a\xc3\xa9rienne</i>, 1909, <a href="/wiki/Grand_Palais" title="Grand Palais">Grand Palais</a>, Paris.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Paris Air Show traces its history to 1908, when a section of the <a href="/wiki/Paris_Motor_Show" title="Paris Motor Show">Paris Motor Show</a> was dedicated to aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\nThe following year, a dedicated air show was held at the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Palais" title="Grand Palais">Grand Palais</a><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> from 25 September to 17 October, during which 100,000 visitors turned out to see products and innovations from 380 exhibitors.<sup id="cite_ref-ParisAirshow_hist_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ParisAirshow_hist-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> There were four further shows before the <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">First World War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>  <span class="citation-needed-content" style="padding-left:0.1em; padding-right:0.1em; color:#595959; border:1px solid #DDD;">The show restarted in 1919, and from 1924 it was held every two years before being interrupted again by the <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">Second World War</a>. It restarted in 1946 and since 1949, has been held in every odd year.</span><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sud_SE-212_Durandal_Le_Bourget_1957.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Sud_SE-212_Durandal_Le_Bourget_1957.jpg/220px-Sud_SE-212_Durandal_Le_Bourget_1957.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Sud_SE-212_Durandal_Le_Bourget_1957.jpg/330px-Sud_SE-212_Durandal_Le_Bourget_1957.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Sud_SE-212_Durandal_Le_Bourget_1957.jpg/440px-Sud_SE-212_Durandal_Le_Bourget_1957.jpg 2x" data-file-width="592" data-file-height="416" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sud_SE-212_Durandal_Le_Bourget_1957.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/SNCASE_SE.212_Durandal" title="SNCASE SE.212 Durandal">SNCASE SE.212 Durandal</a> experimental jet/rocket fighter aircraft at the 1957 Air Salon</div></div></div>\n<p>The air show continued to be held at the Grand Palais, and from 1949 flying demonstrations were staged at Paris <a href="/wiki/Orly_Airport" title="Orly Airport">Orly Airport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> In 1953, the show was relocated from the Grand Palais to Le Bourget.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> The show was drawing international notice in the 1960s.<sup id="cite_ref-UPI_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UPI-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Since the 1970s, the show has emerged as the main international reference of the aeronautical sector.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1967">1967</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paris_Air_Show&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: 1967">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The 1967 air show was opened by French President <a href="/wiki/Charles_de_Gaulle" title="Charles de Gaulle">Charles de Gaulle</a>, who toured the exhibits and shook hands with two Soviet <a href="/wiki/Astronaut" title="Astronaut">cosmonauts</a> and two American <a href="/wiki/Astronauts" class="mw-redirect" title="Astronauts">astronauts</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UPI_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UPI-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\nProminently displayed by the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> was a three-stage <a href="/wiki/Vostok_(rocket_family)" title="Vostok (rocket family)">Vostok rocket</a>, such as the one that had carried <a href="/wiki/Yuri_Gagarin" title="Yuri Gagarin">Yuri Gagarin</a> into space on April 12, 1961. The "extraordinarily powerful" Vostok was downplayed by American missile experts as "rather old and unsophisticated."<sup id="cite_ref-Mooney_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mooney-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> The American exhibit, the largest at the fair, featured the <a href="/wiki/F-111" class="mw-redirect" title="F-111">F-111</a> swing-wing fighter bomber,<sup id="cite_ref-Mooney_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mooney-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> a replica of <a href="/wiki/Charles_Lindberg" class="mw-redirect" title="Charles Lindberg">Charles Lindbergh\'s</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Spirit_of_St._Louis" title="Spirit of St. Louis">Spirit of St. Louis</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/LTV_XC-142A" class="mw-redirect" title="LTV XC-142A">Ling-Temco-Vought XC-142A</a>, a cargo plane capable of a vertical takeoff and landing.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\nA full-size model of the supersonic <a href="/wiki/Concorde" title="Concorde">Concorde</a> was displayed by the French and British,<sup id="cite_ref-Mooney_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mooney-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> auguring its successful first flight on March 2, 1969.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1969">1969</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paris_Air_Show&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1969">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>"The largest plane in the world," the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747" title="Boeing 747">Boeing 747</a> jet airliner, arrived on June 3, after flying non-stop from <a href="/wiki/Seattle" title="Seattle">Seattle</a>, Washington,<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Apollo_8" title="Apollo 8">Apollo 8</a> command module, charred by its re-entry, was there flanked by the <a href="/wiki/Apollo_9" title="Apollo 9">Apollo 9</a> astronauts, but the most-viewed exhibit was the supersonic <a href="/wiki/Concorde" title="Concorde">Concorde</a>, which made its first flight over Paris as the show opened.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1971">1971</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paris_Air_Show&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1971">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The Soviet <a href="/wiki/TU-144" class="mw-redirect" title="TU-144">TU-144</a> supersonic airliner was flown to <a href="/wiki/Le_Bourget" title="Le Bourget">Le Bourget</a> for the 1971 show,<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> drawing comparisons with the French <a href="/wiki/Concorde" title="Concorde">Concorde</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Landing with the Concorde was the world\'s largest aircraft, the American <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_C-5_Galaxy" title="Lockheed C-5 Galaxy">Lockheed C-5A Galaxy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1973">1973</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paris_Air_Show&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 1973">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/1973_Paris_Air_Show_Tu-144_crash" title="1973 Paris Air Show Tu-144 crash">crash of the Soviet Tu-144</a>, see below, overshadowed the 1973 show, otherwise characterized by "There was nothing new", although the flying was memorable,<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> and there were a great many exhibits.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1975">1975</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paris_Air_Show&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 1975">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>One hundred and eighty-two aircraft were scheduled for appearance.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Despite restrictions that followed the <a href="/wiki/1973_Paris_Air_Show_Tu-144_crash" title="1973 Paris Air Show Tu-144 crash">TU-144 crash in 1973</a>, a day of flying pleased viewers. In particular, the American <a href="/wiki/General_Dynamics_F-16_Fighting_Falcon" title="General Dynamics F-16 Fighting Falcon">YF-16</a> and the French <a href="/wiki/Dassault_Mirage_F1" title="Dassault Mirage F1">Mirage F-1E</a> competed in turn before a critical audience.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Days later, Belgium became the fourth European nation to choose the YF-16 over the F-1E.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1977">1977</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paris_Air_Show&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 1977">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Celebration of <a href="/wiki/Charles_Lindberg" class="mw-redirect" title="Charles Lindberg">Charles Lindbergh\'s</a> trans-Atlantic flight to Le Bourget fifty years ago recalled that historic event.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Anne_Morrow_Lindbergh" title="Anne Morrow Lindbergh">Anne Morrow Lindbergh</a>, Lindbergh\'s widow, attended the ceremony along with early trans-Atlantic pilots, <a href="/wiki/Maurice_Bellonte" title="Maurice Bellonte">Maurice Bellonte</a> and Armand Lotti.<sup id="cite_ref-Lindbergh_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lindbergh-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Recent extension of <a href="/wiki/Exclusive_economic_zone" title="Exclusive economic zone">coastal limits</a> to 200 nautical miles has produced new <a href="/wiki/Maritime_patrol_aircraft" title="Maritime patrol aircraft">maritime-reconnaissance (MR) aircraft</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> The crash of a <a href="/wiki/Fairchild_Republic_A-10_Thunderbolt_II" title="Fairchild Republic A-10 Thunderbolt II">Fairchild A-10 tank-destroyer</a><sup id="cite_ref-Lindbergh_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lindbergh-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> led to tightened rules on air show demonstrations.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1979">1979</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paris_Air_Show&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 1979">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Two airliners, the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A310" title="Airbus A310">Airbus A310</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_767" title="Boeing 767">Boeing 767</a>, are competing for the international market, but neither will carry passengers before 1982.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Westland_30" title="Westland 30">Westland WG30</a> transport helicopter shows promise.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> "The <a href="/wiki/Dassault_Mirage_4000" title="Dassault Mirage 4000">Mirage 4000</a> remains a question mark"<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> despite being "surely the main highlight this year at Le Bourget."<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1981">1981</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paris_Air_Show&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 1981">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Exhibiting at the show, <a href="/wiki/Airbus_320_family" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus 320 family">Airbus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737_Next_Generation" title="Boeing 737 Next Generation">Boeing</a>, and <a href="/wiki/McDonnell_Douglas" title="McDonnell Douglas">McDonnell Douglas</a>/<a href="/wiki/Fokker" title="Fokker">Fokker</a> vie for the 150-seat airline market, while <a href="/wiki/Rolls-Royce_plc" class="mw-redirect" title="Rolls-Royce plc">Rolls Royce/Japan</a>, <a href="/wiki/CFM_International_CFM56" title="CFM International CFM56">General Electric/Snecma (CFM)</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pratt_%26_Whitney" title="Pratt &amp; Whitney">Pratt &amp; Whitney</a> contest for their engines.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Northrop_F-5" title="Northrop F-5">Northrop F-5G Tigershark</a> mockup was on display and expected to fly in 1982 with delivery the following year. A novelty was Air Transat, a light aircraft trans-Atlantic race from <a href="/wiki/Le_Bourget" title="Le Bourget">Le Bourget</a> to <a href="/wiki/Sikorsky_Memorial_Airport" title="Sikorsky Memorial Airport">Sikorsky Memorial Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bridgeport" class="mw-redirect" title="Bridgeport">Bridgeport</a>, Connecticut and back,<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> won by a twin engine <a href="/wiki/Piper_PA-31_Navajo" title="Piper PA-31 Navajo">Piper Navaho</a><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> and a <a href="/wiki/Beechcraft_Bonanza" title="Beechcraft Bonanza">Beechcraft Bonanza</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1983">1983</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paris_Air_Show&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 1983">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The American <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Enterprise" title="Space Shuttle Enterprise">Space Shuttle <i>Enterprise</i></a> was flown around Paris and towered over other exhibits,<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> but "much more intriguing"<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> were replicas of two twin-engined fighters, the <a href="/wiki/British_Aerospace_EAP" title="British Aerospace EAP">British Aerospace ACA</a><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> and French <a href="/wiki/Dassault_Rafale" title="Dassault Rafale">Dassault Breguet ACX</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Sales of <a href="/wiki/Boeing_757" title="Boeing 757">Boeing 757</a> and <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A310" title="Airbus A310">Airbus A310</a> airliners to <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Airlines" title="Singapore Airlines">Singapore Airlines</a> were welcome news during an ongoing recession.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1985">1985</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paris_Air_Show&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: 1985">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The Soviet <a href="/wiki/Antonov_An-124_Ruslan" title="Antonov An-124 Ruslan">Antonov An-124 Ruslan</a> military heavy lifter was the largest exhibit in 1985.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Propfan" title="Propfan">Propfan</a> engines stirred interest.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> Reflecting the upturn in the economy, <a href="/wiki/Boeing" title="Boeing">Boeing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Airbus" title="Airbus">Airbus</a> announced new contracts totaling as much as $1,700&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Hubble_Space_Telescope" title="Hubble Space Telescope">Hubble Space Telescope</a><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> should be deployed in 1986.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1987">1987</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paris_Air_Show&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: 1987">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Newly introduced, in the rain, were the Soviet <a href="/wiki/Mil_Mi-34" title="Mil Mi-34">Mil Mi-34</a> Helicopter,<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> the Israeli Super Phantom,<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> and the Harrier GR.5.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Airbus" title="Airbus">Airbus</a> announced firm orders for both the <a href="/wiki/A330" class="mw-redirect" title="A330">A330</a> and <a href="/wiki/A340" class="mw-redirect" title="A340">A340</a> airliners.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> Exhibiting at the show for the first time, the Chinese displayed, among others, the <a href="/wiki/Nanchang_Q-5" title="Nanchang Q-5">A-5C Attacker (Fantan)</a> and FT-7.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dick_Rutan" title="Dick Rutan">Richard Rutan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jeana_Yeager" title="Jeana Yeager">Jeana Yeager</a>, who flew a <a href="/wiki/Rutan_Voyager" title="Rutan Voyager">Voyager</a> non-stop around the world without refueling, were present, but their aircraft was not.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1989">1989</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paris_Air_Show&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: 1989">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Antonov_An-225_with_Buran_at_Le_Bourget_1989_Manteufel.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Antonov_An-225_with_Buran_at_Le_Bourget_1989_Manteufel.jpg/220px-Antonov_An-225_with_Buran_at_Le_Bourget_1989_Manteufel.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Antonov_An-225_with_Buran_at_Le_Bourget_1989_Manteufel.jpg/330px-Antonov_An-225_with_Buran_at_Le_Bourget_1989_Manteufel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Antonov_An-225_with_Buran_at_Le_Bourget_1989_Manteufel.jpg/440px-Antonov_An-225_with_Buran_at_Le_Bourget_1989_Manteufel.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="682" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Antonov_An-225_with_Buran_at_Le_Bourget_1989_Manteufel.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Antonov_An-225_Mriya" title="Antonov An-225 Mriya">Antonov An-225 Mriya</a> with <a href="/wiki/Buran_programme" title="Buran programme">Buran</a> at Le Bourget, 1989</div></div></div>\n<p>The "38th Paris International Air and Space Show" or "1989 Paris Air Show", featured a variety of aerospace technology from <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> and <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Pact" title="Warsaw Pact">Warsaw Pact</a> nations.<sup id="cite_ref-buran_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-buran-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\nA <a href="/wiki/Mikoyan_MiG-29" title="Mikoyan MiG-29">Mikoyan MiG-29</a> crashed during a demonstration flight with no loss of life.  The then-Soviet space shuttle <a href="/wiki/Buran_(spacecraft)" title="Buran (spacecraft)">Buran</a> and its carrier, <a href="/wiki/Antonov_An-225_Mriya" title="Antonov An-225 Mriya">Antonov An-225 Mriya</a>, was displayed at this show.<sup id="cite_ref-buran_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-buran-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\nA <a href="/wiki/Sukhoi_Su-27" title="Sukhoi Su-27">Sukhoi Su-27</a> made debut to western world, as well first publicly seen "Cobra" maneuver.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1991">1991</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paris_Air_Show&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: 1991">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Despite a <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Defense" title="United States Department of Defense">Department of Defense</a> display of the F-117A Stealth Fighter and other <a href="/wiki/Gulf_War" title="Gulf War">Gulf War</a> armaments,<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> most American contractors stayed home, so Soviet aircraft drew attention,<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> among them the <a href="/wiki/Beriev_A-40" title="Beriev A-40">Beriev Be-42 Mermaid (A-40 Albatros)</a> amphibian,<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Mikoyan_MiG-31" title="Mikoyan MiG-31">MiG-31 Foxhound</a> interceptor,<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Yakovlev_Yak-141" title="Yakovlev Yak-141">Yak-141</a> short take-off/vertical landing (ASTOVL) supersonic fighter.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> When it receives its first customer order, Dassault plans to begin production of the <a href="/wiki/Mirage_2000-5" class="mw-redirect" title="Mirage 2000-5">Mirage 2000-5</a>, which is a "new machine compared to the basic <a href="/wiki/Mirage_2000" class="mw-redirect" title="Mirage 2000">Mirage 2000</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1993">1993</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paris_Air_Show&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: 1993">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The show attracted 1,611 exhibitors from 39 countries and nearly 300,000 visitors attended the show.<sup id="cite_ref-Flight10May1995_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flight10May1995-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dassault_Group" title="Dassault Group">Dassault</a> featured the debut of the <a href="/wiki/Dassault_Falcon_2000" title="Dassault Falcon 2000">Falcon 2000</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Airbus" title="Airbus">Airbus</a> will manufacture the 130-seat <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A319" title="Airbus A319">A319</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1995">1995</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paris_Air_Show&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: 1995">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:B-2_Spirit_at_Le_Bourget_Airport.JPEG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/B-2_Spirit_at_Le_Bourget_Airport.JPEG/220px-B-2_Spirit_at_Le_Bourget_Airport.JPEG" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/B-2_Spirit_at_Le_Bourget_Airport.JPEG/330px-B-2_Spirit_at_Le_Bourget_Airport.JPEG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/B-2_Spirit_at_Le_Bourget_Airport.JPEG/440px-B-2_Spirit_at_Le_Bourget_Airport.JPEG 2x" data-file-width="2937" data-file-height="1950" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:B-2_Spirit_at_Le_Bourget_Airport.JPEG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A stealth <a href="/wiki/B-2_Spirit" class="mw-redirect" title="B-2 Spirit">B-2 Spirit</a> in 1995</div></div></div>\n<p>The 41st Paris Air Show main attraction was the stealth <a href="/wiki/B-2_Spirit" class="mw-redirect" title="B-2 Spirit">B-2 Spirit</a> bomber, along with the <a href="/wiki/Tupolev_Tu-160" title="Tupolev Tu-160">Tupolev Tu-160</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sukhoi_Su-32" class="mw-redirect" title="Sukhoi Su-32">Sukhoi Su-32</a> bombers.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>\nThe flying display included the <a href="/wiki/Bell-Boeing_V-22" class="mw-redirect" title="Bell-Boeing V-22">Bell-Boeing V-22</a> tilt-rotor, the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_Beluga" title="Airbus Beluga">Airbus Beluga</a> Super Transporter, the <a href="/wiki/Eurofighter_2000" class="mw-redirect" title="Eurofighter 2000">Eurofighter 2000</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Rockwell-MBB_X-31" title="Rockwell-MBB X-31">Rockwell-MBB X-31</a> high-manoeuvrability fighter demonstrator, the <a href="/wiki/McDonnell_Douglas_C-17" class="mw-redirect" title="McDonnell Douglas C-17">McDonnell Douglas C-17</a> military transport, the <a href="/wiki/Eurocopter_EC135" title="Eurocopter EC135">Eurocopter EC135</a> civil helicopter, the <a href="/wiki/Sukhoi_Su-35" title="Sukhoi Su-35">Sukhoi Su-35</a> fighter, and the Daimler-Benz Aerospace <a href="/wiki/Dornier_328" title="Dornier 328">Dornier 328</a>-100, and for the first time on static  the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_777" title="Boeing 777">Boeing 777</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saab_Gripen" class="mw-redirect" title="Saab Gripen">Saab Gripen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Atlas_Cheetah" title="Atlas Cheetah">Atlas Cheetah</a> Mirage and <a href="/wiki/Cessna_Citation_X" title="Cessna Citation X">Cessna Citation X</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Flight10May1995_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flight10May1995-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1997">1997</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paris_Air_Show&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: 1997">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/American_Eagle_(airline_brand)" title="American Eagle (airline brand)">America Eagle</a> announced purchase of forty-two <a href="/wiki/EMB-145" class="mw-redirect" title="EMB-145">EMB-145</a> regional jets from <a href="/wiki/Embraer" title="Embraer">Embraer</a> and twenty-five <a href="/wiki/Bombardier_CRJ700" class="mw-redirect" title="Bombardier CRJ700">Bombardier CRJ700</a> airliners from <a href="/wiki/Bombardier_Aerospace" class="mw-redirect" title="Bombardier Aerospace">Bombardier</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> Spectators saw two <a href="/wiki/Eurofighter_Typhoon" title="Eurofighter Typhoon">Eurofighter Typhoon EF2000s</a> flying together.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> A full-scale mock-up of the <a href="/wiki/AgustaWestland_AW609" title="AgustaWestland AW609">Bell Boeing 609</a> civil <a href="/wiki/Tiltrotor" title="Tiltrotor">tilt-rotor</a> aircraft attracted attention.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Industria_Aeronautic%C4%83_Rom%C3%A2n%C4%83" title="Industria Aeronautic\xc4\x83 Rom\xc3\xa2n\xc4\x83">IAR Brasov</a> featured a prototype Anti-Tank Optronic Search and Combat System (SOCAT) helicopter, an upgrade of the <a href="/wiki/IAR_330" title="IAR 330">IAR-330 Puma</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1999">1999</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paris_Air_Show&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: 1999">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The 1999 show continued a trend away from displays of new aircraft toward announcements of new contracts.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> Although new entries such as the <a href="/wiki/Fairchild_Dornier_328JET" title="Fairchild Dornier 328JET">Fairchild 30-seat 328JET</a><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_717" title="Boeing 717">Boeing 100-seat 717-200</a>\n<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> attracted interest, airlines ordered as many as 103 <a href="/wiki/Embraer_ERJ_family" title="Embraer ERJ family">Embraer ERJ-135s and 145s</a> in addition to a 4.9&#160;billion-dollar order for <a href="/wiki/Embraer_E-Jet_family" title="Embraer E-Jet family">ERJ-170s and ERJ-190</a>-200s.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> In February, the Russian <a href="/wiki/Ilyushin_Il-103" title="Ilyushin Il-103">Il-103</a> received US Federal Aviation Administration (FAA) approval, a breakthrough in certifying Russian aircraft for the American market.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> Subsequent certification for the <a href="/wiki/Ilyushin_Il-96" title="Ilyushin Il-96">Ilyushin Il-96T</a> wide-bodied jet was displayed at the show.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2001">2001</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paris_Air_Show&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: 2001">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Boeing introduced scale models of their <a href="/wiki/Boeing_Sonic_Cruiser" title="Boeing Sonic Cruiser">Sonic Cruiser</a> which would reach speeds approaching Mach 0.98,<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> together with a walk-through hologram.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380" title="Airbus A380">Airbus A380</a>, seating 555, offered size rather than speed, and was there on the tarmac.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> Crowds toured the restored <a href="/wiki/Antonov_An-225_Mriya" title="Antonov An-225 Mriya">Antonov An-225 Dream</a>, the world\'s largest aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dassault_Group" title="Dassault Group">Dassault</a> featured a model of the new <a href="/wiki/Dassault_Falcon_7X" title="Dassault Falcon 7X">Falcon FNX</a> business jet that is projected to fly 10,500 kilometers at Mach 0.88.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Joint_Strike_Fighter_program" title="Joint Strike Fighter program">The Joint Strike Fighter (JSF)</a>, which is undergoing <a href="/wiki/STOVL" title="STOVL">STOVL</a> testing, is a likely replacement for older American <a href="/wiki/McDonnell_Douglas_F-15E_Strike_Eagle" title="McDonnell Douglas F-15E Strike Eagle">F-15E Strike Eagles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_F-117_Nighthawk" title="Lockheed F-117 Nighthawk">F-117 Nighthawks</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2003">2003</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paris_Air_Show&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: 2003">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Concorde" title="Concorde">Concorde F-BTSD</a> made its farewell landing at <a href="/wiki/Le_Bourget" title="Le Bourget">Le Bourget</a> on June 14, the opening day,<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Dassault_Mirage_2000" title="Dassault Mirage 2000">Dassault\'s Mirage 2000</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dassault_Rafale" title="Dassault Rafale">Rafale</a> put on a show overhead.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> Pilotless planes, such as the <a href="/wiki/Northrop_Grumman_RQ-4_Global_Hawk" title="Northrop Grumman RQ-4 Global Hawk">Northrop Grumman RQ-4 Global Hawk</a><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/General_Atomics_MQ-1_Predator" title="General Atomics MQ-1 Predator">General Atomics Predator</a> drew attention.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> Boeing publicized the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_787_Dreamliner" title="Boeing 787 Dreamliner">7E7 Dreamliner</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2005">2005</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paris_Air_Show&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: 2005">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Flightglobal" class="mw-redirect" title="Flightglobal">FlightGlobal</a> cited the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380" title="Airbus A380">Airbus A380</a><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> and "nineteen remarkable first appearances," including <a href="/wiki/Dassault_Falcon_7X" title="Dassault Falcon 7X">Dassault\'s Falcon 7X</a><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Gulfstream_G550" title="Gulfstream G550">Gulfstream\'s G550</a><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> business jets, <a href="/wiki/Embraer_E-Jet_family" title="Embraer E-Jet family">Embraer\'s EMB-195</a> regional jet,<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> and the second prototype of <a href="/wiki/Alenia_Aermacchi_M-346_Master" title="Alenia Aermacchi M-346 Master">Alenia Aermacchi\'s M-346</a><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> advanced jet trainer.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Birch_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Birch-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> CompositesWorld added the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_777" title="Boeing 777">Boeing 777-200LR</a><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Dassault_nEUROn" title="Dassault nEUROn">Dassault UCAV Neuron</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2007">2007</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paris_Air_Show&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: 2007">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Boeing_787_Dreamliner" title="Boeing 787 Dreamliner">Boeing 787 Dreamliner</a><sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> sold briskly, as did the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380" title="Airbus A380">Airbus A380</a><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A350_XWB" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A350 XWB">A350 XWB</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> A mockup of the <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_Martin_F-35_Lightning_II" title="Lockheed Martin F-35 Lightning II">Lockheed Martin Joint Strike Fighter</a><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> was on display. The <a href="/wiki/Israel_Aerospace_Industries" title="Israel Aerospace Industries">IAI</a> <a href="/wiki/IAI_Eitan" title="IAI Eitan">Heron TP</a> <a href="/wiki/Unmanned_aerial_vehicle" title="Unmanned aerial vehicle">UAV</a><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> is ready to enter production. The Spanish steer-by-leaning AN-1 AeroQuad flying platform from Aeris Naviter weighed only 100 kilograms.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2009">2009</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paris_Air_Show&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: 2009">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The 48th International Paris Air Show took place in 2009 and marked a hundred years of technological innovation in aeronautics and space conquest. The event was held from 15 to 21 June, at Le Bourget. A memorial service was held for the victims of <a href="/wiki/Air_France_Flight_447" title="Air France Flight 447">Air France Flight 447</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Pressrelchurch0_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pressrelchurch0-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2011">2011</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paris_Air_Show&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: 2011">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Solarimpulsebourget.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Solarimpulsebourget.jpg/220px-Solarimpulsebourget.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Solarimpulsebourget.jpg/330px-Solarimpulsebourget.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Solarimpulsebourget.jpg/440px-Solarimpulsebourget.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4928" data-file-height="3264" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Solarimpulsebourget.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Solar_Impulse" title="Solar Impulse">Solar Impulse</a> at Le Bourget 2011</div></div></div>\n<p>The 2011 show was the 49th presentation, and hosted over 2,100 international exhibitors in 28 international pavilions. A total of 150 aircraft were on display, including the solar-electric aircraft <a href="/wiki/Solar_Impulse" title="Solar Impulse">Solar Impulse</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A demo A380 was damaged the day before the exhibition opened and needed a replacement;<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-demoprobleme_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-demoprobleme-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> while the new <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A400M_Atlas" title="Airbus A400M Atlas">Airbus A400M Atlas</a> military transport aircraft had an engine failure, but could still perform some demonstration flights.<sup id="cite_ref-demoprobleme_111-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-demoprobleme-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2015">2015</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paris_Air_Show&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: 2015">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The 2015 show, held from June 15 to June 21, 2015, saw the new <a href="/wiki/Dassault_Falcon_8X" class="mw-redirect" title="Dassault Falcon 8X">Dassault Falcon 8X</a>, <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A350_XWB" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A350 XWB">Airbus A350 XWB</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bombardier_CS300" class="mw-redirect" title="Bombardier CS300">Bombardier CS300</a> and received 351,584 visitors, 2,303 exhibitors over 122,500 <a href="/wiki/Square_metre" title="Square metre">square metres</a> of exhibition space, 4,359 journalists from 72 countries and 130&#160;billion euros in purchases and "cemented its position as the world\'s largest event dedicated to the aerospace industry".<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>\nDuring the show, Airbus Helicopters announced a successor to the <a href="/wiki/Eurocopter_AS332_Super_Puma" title="Eurocopter AS332 Super Puma">Super Puma</a>, called the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_Helicopters_X6" title="Airbus Helicopters X6">Airbus Helicopters X6</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2017">2017</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paris_Air_Show&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: 2017">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Paris_Air_Show_2017_Airbus_racer_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Paris_Air_Show_2017_Airbus_racer_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Paris_Air_Show_2017_Airbus_racer_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="102" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Paris_Air_Show_2017_Airbus_racer_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Paris_Air_Show_2017_Airbus_racer_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Paris_Air_Show_2017_Airbus_racer_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Paris_Air_Show_2017_Airbus_racer_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2896" data-file-height="1347" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Paris_Air_Show_2017_Airbus_racer_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Airbus_Helicopters_X3" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus Helicopters X3">Airbus Helicopters X3</a>-derived RACER model, 2017</div></div></div>\n<p>The 52nd Air Show was held from 19 to 25 June 2017, with 2,381 exhibitors from 48 countries, showing 140 aircraft including for the first time the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A321neo" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A321neo">Airbus A321neo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A350-1000" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A350-1000">Airbus A350-1000</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boeing_787-10" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 787-10">Boeing 787-10</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737_MAX_9" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 737 MAX 9">Boeing 737 MAX 9</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kawasaki_P-1" title="Kawasaki P-1">Kawasaki P-1</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mitsubishi_MRJ90" class="mw-redirect" title="Mitsubishi MRJ90">Mitsubishi MRJ90</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_Martin_F-35" class="mw-redirect" title="Lockheed Martin F-35">Lockheed Martin F-35</a>.\nInaugurated by French President <a href="/wiki/Emmanuel_Macron" title="Emmanuel Macron">Emmanuel Macron</a>, it was visited by 290 official delegations from 98 countries and 7 international organizations, French Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Edouard_Philippe" class="mw-redirect" title="Edouard Philippe">Edouard Philippe</a>, 3,450 journalists, 142,000 trade visitors and 180,000 general public visitors.\nAnnouncements for 934 commercial aircraft orders and purchasing commitments were worth a catalogue value of US$115&#160;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-28June2017PR_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28June2017PR-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>There were 1,226 order and commitments&#160;: 352 firm orders, 699 letters of intent or memorandums of understanding, 40 options and  135 options letters of intent; plus 229 conversions of existing orders, mainly for the Boeing <a href="/wiki/737-10" class="mw-redirect" title="737-10">737-10</a> MAX variant launched at the show.\nThere were mainly <a href="/wiki/Narrow-body_aircraft" title="Narrow-body aircraft">narrowbodies</a> with 1,021 orders or commitments against 76 <a href="/wiki/Wide-body_aircraft" title="Wide-body aircraft">widebodies</a>, 48 <a href="/wiki/Regional_jet" title="Regional jet">regional jets</a> and 81 <a href="/wiki/Turboprop" title="Turboprop">turboprop</a> airliners.\nWith 766, mainly preliminary deals, <a href="/wiki/Boeing" title="Boeing">Boeing</a> led <a href="/wiki/Airbus" title="Airbus">Airbus</a> with 331, while <a href="/wiki/Bombardier_Aerospace" class="mw-redirect" title="Bombardier Aerospace">Bombardier Aerospace</a> had 64, <a href="/wiki/Embraer" title="Embraer">Embraer</a> 48 and <a href="/wiki/ATR_Aircraft" class="mw-redirect" title="ATR Aircraft">ATR Aircraft</a> 17.\nNearly half of those order and commitments was from <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_lessor" class="mw-redirect" title="Aircraft lessor">aircraft lessors</a> with 513, and where the operator was known, 43% came from Asia-Pacific, 27% from the middle east, 10% from Europe as from South America, 7% from Africa and 3% from North America.<sup id="cite_ref-Flight2017report_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flight2017report-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2019">2019</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paris_Air_Show&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: 2019">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:1102px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Static_display,Paris_Air_Show_2019,_Le_Bourget_(SIAE8871-Pano)_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Static_display%2CParis_Air_Show_2019%2C_Le_Bourget_%28SIAE8871-Pano%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/1100px-Static_display%2CParis_Air_Show_2019%2C_Le_Bourget_%28SIAE8871-Pano%29_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="1100" height="114" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Static_display%2CParis_Air_Show_2019%2C_Le_Bourget_%28SIAE8871-Pano%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/1650px-Static_display%2CParis_Air_Show_2019%2C_Le_Bourget_%28SIAE8871-Pano%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Static_display%2CParis_Air_Show_2019%2C_Le_Bourget_%28SIAE8871-Pano%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/2200px-Static_display%2CParis_Air_Show_2019%2C_Le_Bourget_%28SIAE8871-Pano%29_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6584" data-file-height="684" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Static_display,Paris_Air_Show_2019,_Le_Bourget_(SIAE8871-Pano)_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Paris air show 2019</div></div></div></div>\n<p>The 53rd Air Show was held from 17 to 23 June 2019 with 2,453 exhibitors from 49 countries over 125,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup> (1,350,000&#160;sq&#160;ft) of exhibition space for 140 aircraft shown including the recently certified <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A330neo" title="Airbus A330neo">Airbus A330neo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Boeing_KC-46" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing KC-46">Boeing KC-46</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bombardier_Global_7500" title="Bombardier Global 7500">Bombardier Global 7500</a>, <a href="/wiki/Embraer_Praetor_600" class="mw-redirect" title="Embraer Praetor 600">Embraer Praetor 600</a> and soon to be certified <a href="/wiki/Cessna_Citation_Latitude" title="Cessna Citation Latitude">Cessna Citation Latitude</a>; it saw 316,470 unique visitors (for more than 500,000 entries): 139,840 professional from 185 countries and 176,630 from the general Public plus 2,700 journalists from 87 countries and announcements for $140&#160;billion worth of orders.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>\nThe air show ended with 866 aircraft commitments totalling $60.9&#160;billion (130 firm orders, 562 LoI/MoU, 119 options and 55 options on LoIs): 388 for <a href="/wiki/Airbus" title="Airbus">Airbus</a> including 243 newly launched <a href="/wiki/A321XLR" class="mw-redirect" title="A321XLR">A321XLRs</a> and 85 <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A220" title="Airbus A220">A220s</a>, 232 for <a href="/wiki/Boeing" title="Boeing">Boeing</a> including 200 <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737_MAX" title="Boeing 737 MAX">737 MAXes</a> for IAG, 145 for <a href="/wiki/ATR_(aircraft_manufacturer)" title="ATR (aircraft manufacturer)">ATR</a> and 78 for <a href="/wiki/Embraer" title="Embraer">Embraer</a>; 558 narrowbodies, 62 widebodies, 93 regional jets and 153 turboprops.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2021">2021</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paris_Air_Show&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: 2021">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Due to the <a href="/wiki/Impact_of_the_COVID-19_pandemic_on_aviation" title="Impact of the COVID-19 pandemic on aviation">Impact of the COVID-19 pandemic</a>, the June 2021 Paris Air Show  was cancelled, the next edition will be held in June 2023.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Accidents">Accidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paris_Air_Show&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Accidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1961">1961</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paris_Air_Show&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: 1961">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>A <a href="/wiki/Convair_B-58_Hustler" title="Convair B-58 Hustler">Convair B-58 Hustler</a> crashed while doing low-altitude <a href="/wiki/Aerobatics" title="Aerobatics">aerobatics</a>. The aircraft reportedly flew into a cloud bank, where visual reference was lost, and crashed.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1965">1965</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paris_Air_Show&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: 1965">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Another Convair B-58 crashed while on final approach during an overweight landing. The aircraft touched down short of the runway, killing United States Air Force Lt. Colonel Charles D. Tubbs. Two other crewmen were injured.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1969_2">1969</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paris_Air_Show&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: 1969">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>A <a href="/wiki/FH-1100" class="mw-redirect" title="FH-1100">Fairchild-Hiller FH-1100</a> helicopter crashed killing the pilot. Witnesses of the crash cite seeing "something wrong with the main rotor".<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1973_2">1973</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paris_Air_Show&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: 1973">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/1973_Paris_Air_Show_crash" class="mw-redirect" title="1973 Paris Air Show crash">1973 Paris Air Show crash</a></div>\n<p>At the Paris Air Show on June 3, 1973, the second <a href="/wiki/Tupolev_Tu-144" title="Tupolev Tu-144">Tupolev Tu-144</a> production aircraft (<a href="/wiki/Aircraft_registration" title="Aircraft registration">registration</a> SSSR-77102) crashed during its display. It stalled while attempting a rapid climb. Trying to pull out of the subsequent dive, the aircraft broke up and crashed, destroying 15 houses and killing all six on board and eight on the ground; a further sixty people received serious injuries.\n</p><p>The cause of this accident remains controversial. Theories include: the Tu-144 climbed to avoid a French Mirage <a href="/wiki/Chase_plane" title="Chase plane">chase plane</a> whose pilot was attempting to photograph it; that changes had been made by the ground engineering team to the auto-stabilisation circuits to allow the Tu-144 to outperform the <a href="/wiki/Concorde" title="Concorde">Concorde</a> in the display circuit; and that the crew were attempting a manoeuvre and to outshine the Concorde.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1977_2">1977</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paris_Air_Show&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: 1977">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>An <a href="/wiki/Fairchild_Republic_A-10_Thunderbolt_II" title="Fairchild Republic A-10 Thunderbolt II">A-10 Thunderbolt</a> crashed killing the pilot.<sup id="cite_ref-Lindbergh_30-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lindbergh-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1989_2">1989</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paris_Air_Show&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: 1989">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>A <a href="/wiki/Mikoyan_MiG-29" title="Mikoyan MiG-29">Mikoyan MiG-29</a> crashed during a demonstration flight with no loss of life.<sup id="cite_ref-buran_57-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-buran-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1999_2">1999</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paris_Air_Show&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: 1999">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>A <a href="/wiki/Sukhoi_Su-30MKI" title="Sukhoi Su-30MKI">Sukhoi Su-30MKI</a> crashed during a demonstration flight with no loss of life.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Paris_Air_Show&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r936637989">.mw-parser-output .portal{border:solid #aaa
